<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During the Middle Ages, the Eritrea region was known as <i><a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a></i> ("sea-land"). The name <i>Eritrea</i> is derived from the ancient Greek name for <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> (<span lang="grc"><a href="/wiki/Erythraean_Sea" title="Erythraean Sea">Ἐρυθρὰ Θάλασσα</a> <i>Erythra Thalassa</i></span>, based on the adjective <span lang="grc">ἐρυθρός <i>erythros</i></span> "red"). It was first formally adopted in 1890, with the formation of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a> (<i>Colonia Eritrea</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The territory became the <a href="/wiki/Eritrea_Governorate" title="Eritrea Governorate">Eritrea Governorate</a> within <a href="/wiki/Italian_East_Africa" title="Italian East Africa">Italian East Africa</a> in 1936. Eritrea was annexed by Ethiopia in 1953 (nominally within a <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Ethiopia_and_Eritrea" title="Federation of Ethiopia and Eritrea">federation</a> until 1962) and an <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean Liberation Front">Eritrean Liberation Front</a> formed in 1960. Eritrea gained independence following the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_independence_referendum,_1993" title="Eritrean independence referendum, 1993">1993 referendum</a>, and the name of the new state was defined as <i>State of Eritrea</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Eritrea" title="Constitution of Eritrea">1997 constitution</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Eritrea" title="History of Eritrea">History of Eritrea</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/40px-Ge%27ez.svg.png" width="40" height="22" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/60px-Ge%27ez.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/80px-Ge%27ez.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="219" data-file-height="120" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">You may need <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Ethiopic)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Ethiopic)">rendering support</a> to display the <a href="/wiki/Ge%27ez_script" title="Ge'ez script">Ethiopic text</a> in this article correctly.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>At Buya in Eritrea, one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Hominid" title="Hominid" class="mw-redirect">hominids</a> representing a possible link between <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> and an archaic <i><a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">Homo sapiens</a></i> was found by Italian scientists. Dated to over 1 million years old, it is the oldest skeletal find of its kind and provides a link between hominids and the earliest <a href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_humans" title="Anatomically modern humans">anatomically modern humans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> It is believed that the section of the <a href="/wiki/Danakil_Depression" title="Danakil Depression">Danakil Depression</a> in Eritrea was also a major player in terms of human evolution, and may contain other traces of evolution from <i>Homo erectus</i> hominids to anatomically modern humans.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the last interglacial period, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> coast of Eritrea was occupied by early anatomically modern humans.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid10811218_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid10811218-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> It is believed that the area was on the route out of Africa that some scholars suggest was used by early humans to colonize the rest of the Old World.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1999, the Eritrean Research Project Team composed of Eritrean, Canadian, American, Dutch and French scientists discovered a <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> site with stone and obsidian tools dated to over 125,000 years old near the Bay of Zula south of <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a>, along the Red Sea littoral. The tools are believed to have been used by early humans to harvest marine resources like clams and oysters.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to linguists, the first <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a>-speaking populations arrived in the region during the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> era from the family's proposed <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_Urheimat" title="Afroasiatic Urheimat">urheimat</a> ("original homeland") in the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" title="Nile Valley" class="mw-redirect">Nile Valley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Other scholars propose that the Afroasiatic family developed in situ in the Horn, with its speakers subsequently dispersing from there.<sup id="cite_ref-Blench143144_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blench143144-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Punt">Punt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Punt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Punt" title="Land of Punt">Land of Punt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:156px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_of_punt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Queen_of_punt.jpg" width="154" height="246" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="246" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_of_punt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen Ati, wife of King Perahu of the <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Punt" title="Land of Punt">Land of Punt</a>, as depicted on Pharaoh <a href="/wiki/Hatshepsut" title="Hatshepsut">Hatshepsut</a>'s temple at <a href="/wiki/Deir_el-Bahri" title="Deir el-Bahri" class="mw-redirect">Deir el-Bahri</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Together with <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, northern <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> coast of <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Eritrea is considered the most likely location of the land known to the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egyptians</a> as <i><a href="/wiki/Land_of_Punt" title="Land of Punt">Punt</a></i>, whose first mention dates to the 25th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The ancient Puntites were a nation of people that had close relations with <a href="/wiki/Pharaoh" title="Pharaoh">Pharaonic Egypt</a> during the times of <a href="/wiki/Pharaoh" title="Pharaoh">Pharaoh</a> <a href="/wiki/Sahure" title="Sahure">Sahure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queen_regnant" title="Queen regnant">Queen</a> <a href="/wiki/Hatshepsut" title="Hatshepsut">Hatshepsut</a>.</p>
<p>In 2010, a genetic study was conducted on the mummified remains of <a href="/wiki/Baboon" title="Baboon">baboons</a> that were brought back as gifts from Punt by the ancient Egyptians. Led by a research team from the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Museum" title="Egyptian Museum">Egyptian Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a>, the scientists used oxygen <a href="/wiki/Isotope" title="Isotope">isotope</a> analysis to examine hairs from two baboon mummies that had been preserved in the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>. One of the baboons had distorted isotopic data, so the other's oxygen isotope values were compared to those of present-day baboon specimens from regions of interest. The researchers found that the mummies most closely matched modern baboon specimens in Eritrea and Ethiopia, which they suggested implied that Punt was likely a narrow region that included eastern Ethiopia and all of Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ona_Culture">Ona Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ona Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SembelExcavation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fc/SembelExcavation.jpg/220px-SembelExcavation.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fc/SembelExcavation.jpg/330px-SembelExcavation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/fc/SembelExcavation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SembelExcavation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Excavation of archaeological site outside of <a href="/wiki/Sembel" title="Sembel">Sembel</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Excavations at <a href="/wiki/Sembel" title="Sembel">Sembel</a> found evidence of an ancient pre-<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Aksumite</a> civilization in greater Asmara. This Ona urban culture is believed to have been among the earliest pastoral and agricultural communities in the Horn region. Artefacts at the site have been dated to between 800 BC and 400 BC, contemporaneous with other pre-Aksumite settlements in the Eritrean and Ethiopian highlands during the mid-first millennium BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Schmidt_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmidt-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Additionally, the Ona culture may have had connections with the ancient Land of Punt. In a tomb in <a href="/wiki/Thebes,_Egypt" title="Thebes, Egypt">Thebes</a> dated to the reign of Pharaoh <a href="/wiki/Amenhotep_II" title="Amenhotep II">Amenophis II</a> (Amenhotep II), long-necked pots similar to those made by the Ona people are depicted as part of the cargo in a ship from Punt.<sup id="cite_ref-Avanzini_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avanzini-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gash_Group">Gash Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Gash Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cohaito.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Cohaito.jpeg/220px-Cohaito.jpeg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Cohaito.jpeg/330px-Cohaito.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Cohaito.jpeg/440px-Cohaito.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="749" data-file-height="470" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cohaito.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pre-Axumite monolithic columns in <a href="/wiki/Qohaito" title="Qohaito">Qohaito</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Excavations in and near <a href="/wiki/Agordat" title="Agordat">Agordat</a> in central Eritrea yielded the remains of an ancient pre-Aksumite civilization known as the Gash Group.<sup id="cite_ref-Leclant402_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leclant402-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Ceramics were discovered that were related to those of the <a href="/wiki/C-Group_Culture" title="C-Group Culture">C-Group</a> (Temehu) pastoral culture, which inhabited the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" title="Nile Valley" class="mw-redirect">Nile Valley</a> between 2500–1500 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Cole_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cole-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Sherds akin to those of the <a href="/wiki/Kerma_Culture" title="Kerma Culture">Kerma</a> culture, another community that flourished in the Nile Valley around the same period, were also found at other local archaeological sites in the Barka valley belonging to the Gash Group.<sup id="cite_ref-Leclant402_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leclant402-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Peter Behrens (1981) and Marianne Bechaus-Gerst (2000), linguistic evidence indicates that the C-Group and Kerma peoples spoke <a href="/wiki/Afro-Asiatic_languages" title="Afro-Asiatic languages" class="mw-redirect">Afro-Asiatic languages</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branches, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Bechaus-Gerst_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bechaus-Gerst-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lbant_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lbant-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_D.27mt">Kingdom of D'mt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Kingdom of D'mt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/D%CA%BFmt" title="Dʿmt">Dʿmt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Africa_in_400_BC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Africa_in_400_BC.jpg/220px-Africa_in_400_BC.jpg" width="220" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Africa_in_400_BC.jpg/330px-Africa_in_400_BC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/Africa_in_400_BC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="361" data-file-height="331" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Africa_in_400_BC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/D%27mt" title="D'mt" class="mw-redirect">D'mt</a> in Eritrea and northern <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, circa 400 BC.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/D%CA%BFmt" title="Dʿmt">Dʿmt</a> was a kingdom that encompassed most of Eritrea and the northern frontier of Ethiopia. The polity existed during the 8th and 7th centuries BC. Given the presence of a massive temple complex, its capital was most likely <a href="/wiki/Yeha" title="Yeha">Yeha</a>. <a href="/wiki/Qohaito" title="Qohaito">Qohaito</a>, often identified as the town of Koloe in the <i><a href="/wiki/Periplus_of_the_Erythraean_Sea" title="Periplus of the Erythraean Sea">Periplus of the Erythraean Sea</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Matara,_Eritrea" title="Matara, Eritrea">Matara</a> were important ancient Dʿmt kingdom cities in southern Eritrea.</p>
<p>The realm developed <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> schemes, used <a href="/wiki/Plow" title="Plow" class="mw-redirect">plows</a>, grew <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, and made <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a> tools and weapons. After the fall of Dʿmt in the 5th century BC, the plateau came to be dominated by smaller successor kingdoms. This lasted until the rise of one of these polities during the first century, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a>, which was able to reunite the area.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Aksum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LocationAksumiteEmpire.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/LocationAksumiteEmpire.png/220px-LocationAksumiteEmpire.png" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/LocationAksumiteEmpire.png/330px-LocationAksumiteEmpire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/LocationAksumiteEmpire.png 2x" data-file-width="397" data-file-height="295" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LocationAksumiteEmpire.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a>'s realm</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Kingdom of Aksum was a trading empire centered in Eritrea and northern Ethiopia.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> It existed from approximately 100–940 AD, growing from the proto-Aksumite <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> period c. 4th century BC to achieve prominence by the 1st century AD.</p>
<p>According to the medieval <i>Liber Axumae</i> (<a href="/wiki/Book_of_Aksum" title="Book of Aksum">Book of Aksum</a>), Aksum's first capital, Mazaber, was built by Itiyopis, son of Cush.<sup id="cite_ref-Agrvt_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agrvt-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The capital was later moved to <a href="/wiki/Axum" title="Axum">Aksum</a> in northern Ethiopia. The Kingdom used the name "Ethiopia" as early as the 4th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Munro-Hay57_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munro-Hay57-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paul_B._Henze_2005_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paul_B._Henze_2005-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Aksumites erected a number of large <a href="/wiki/Stele" title="Stele">stelae</a>, which served a religious purpose in pre-<a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> times. One of these granite columns is the largest such structure in the world, standing at 90 feet.<sup id="cite_ref-Eospvo_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eospvo-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Ezana_of_Axum" title="Ezana of Axum">Ezana</a> (<a href="/wiki/Floruit" title="Floruit">fl.</a> 320–360), Aksum later adopted <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Munro-Hay_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munro-Hay-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 7th century, early <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a> also sought refuge from <a href="/wiki/Quraysh_(tribe)" title="Quraysh (tribe)" class="mw-redirect">Quraysh</a> persecution by travelling to the kingdom, a journey known in <a href="/wiki/Islamic_history" title="Islamic history" class="mw-redirect">Islamic history</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Migration_to_Abyssinia" title="Migration to Abyssinia">First Hijra</a>. It is also the alleged resting place of the <a href="/wiki/Ark_of_the_Covenant" title="Ark of the Covenant">Ark of the Covenant</a> and the purported home of the <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Sheba" title="Queen of Sheba">Queen of Sheba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The kingdom is mentioned in the <i>Periplus of the Erythraean Sea</i> as an important market place for <a href="/wiki/Ivory_trade" title="Ivory trade">ivory</a>, which was exported throughout the ancient world. Aksum was at the time ruled by <a href="/wiki/Zoskales" title="Zoskales">Zoskales</a>, who also governed the port of <a href="/wiki/Adulis" title="Adulis">Adulis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Periplusme_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Periplusme-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The Aksumite rulers facilitated trade by minting their own <a href="/wiki/Aksumite_currency" title="Aksumite currency">Aksumite currency</a>. The state also established its <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a> over the declining <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kush" title="Kingdom of Kush">Kingdom of Kush</a> and regularly entered the politics of the kingdoms on the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_peninsula" title="Arabian peninsula" class="mw-redirect">Arabian peninsula</a>, eventually extending its rule over the region with the conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Himyarite_Kingdom" title="Himyarite Kingdom">Himyarite Kingdom</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medri_Bahri">Medri Bahri</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Medri Bahri">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea-Semenawi_Keyih_Bahri.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/Eritrea-Semenawi_Keyih_Bahri.png" width="200" height="176" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="176" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea-Semenawi_Keyih_Bahri.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Red_Sea_Region" title="Northern Red Sea Region">Northern Red Sea Region</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Hamasien" title="Hamasien">Hamasien</a> province of the medieval <a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a> kingdom.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the decline of Aksum, the Eritrean highlands were under the domain of <a href="/wiki/Bahr_Negash" title="Bahr Negash" class="mw-redirect">Bahr Negash</a> ruled by the Bahr Negus. The area was then known as <i>Ma'ikele Bahr</i> ("between the seas/rivers," i.e. the land between the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mareb_River" title="Mareb River">Mereb river</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> It was later renamed under Emperor <a href="/wiki/Zara_Yaqob" title="Zara Yaqob">Zara Yaqob</a> as the domain of the Bahr Negash, the <a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a> ("Sea land" in Tingrinya, although it included some areas like <a href="/wiki/Shire,_Ethiopia" title="Shire, Ethiopia">Shire</a> on the other side of the Mereb, today in Ethiopia).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> With its capital at <a href="/wiki/Debarwa" title="Debarwa">Debarwa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> the state's main provinces were <a href="/wiki/Hamasien" title="Hamasien">Hamasien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serae" title="Serae">Serae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Akele_Guzai" title="Akele Guzai">Akele Guzai</a>.</p>
<p>The Scottish traveler <a href="/wiki/James_Bruce" title="James Bruce">James Bruce</a> reported in 1770 that Medri Bahri was a distinct political entity from <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Abyssinia</a>, noting that the two territories were frequently in conflict. The Bahre-Nagassi ("Kings of the Sea") alternately fought with or against the Abyssinians and the neighbouring Muslim <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">Adal Sultanate</a> depending on the geopolitical circumstances. Medri Bahri was thus part of the Christian resistance against Imam <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_ibn_Ibrahim_al-Ghazi" title="Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Ghazi">Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Ghazi</a> of Adal's forces, but later joined the Adalite states and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> front against Abyssinia in 1572. That 16th century also marked the arrival of the Ottomans, who began making inroads in the Red Sea area.<sup id="cite_ref-MB01_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB01-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Habesh_Eyalet">Habesh Eyalet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Habesh Eyalet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Habesh_Eyalet" title="Habesh Eyalet">Habesh Eyalet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OttomanEmpireIn1683.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/OttomanEmpireIn1683.png/220px-OttomanEmpireIn1683.png" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/OttomanEmpireIn1683.png/330px-OttomanEmpireIn1683.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/OttomanEmpireIn1683.png/440px-OttomanEmpireIn1683.png 2x" data-file-width="1966" data-file-height="1850" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OttomanEmpireIn1683.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1683</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 1517, the Ottomans had succeeded in conquering Medri Bahri. They occupied all of northeastern present-day Eritrea for the next two decades, an area which stretched from <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> to <a href="/wiki/Suakin" title="Suakin">Swakin</a> in Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-MB01_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB01-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The territory became an Ottoman province or <a href="/wiki/Eyalet" title="Eyalet">eyalet</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Habesh_Eyalet" title="Habesh Eyalet">Habesh Eyalet</a>. Massawa served as the new province's first capital. When the city became of secondary economical importance, the administrative capital was soon moved across the Red Sea to <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>. Its headquarters remained there from the end of the 16th century to the early 19th century, with Medina temporarily serving as the capital in the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-encaet_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encaet-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Ottomans were eventually driven out in the last quarter of the 16th century. However, they retained control over the seaboard until the establishment of Italian Eritrea in the late 1800s.<sup id="cite_ref-MB01_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB01-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aussa_Sultanate">Aussa Sultanate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Aussa Sultanate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aussa" title="Sultanate of Aussa">Sultanate of Aussa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Red.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Red_Red.svg/220px-Red_Red.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Red_Red.svg/330px-Red_Red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Red_Red.svg/440px-Red_Red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="324" data-file-height="217" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Red.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flag of the <a href="/wiki/Aussa_Sultanate" title="Aussa Sultanate" class="mw-redirect">Aussa Sultanate</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Aussa_Sultanate" title="Aussa Sultanate" class="mw-redirect">Aussa Sultanate</a> was established in the Denkel lowlands of Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-Aesna_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aesna-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The polity had come into existence in 1577, when Muhammed Jasa moved his capital from <a href="/wiki/Harar" title="Harar">Harar</a> to <a href="/wiki/Asaita" title="Asaita">Aussa</a> (Asaita) with the split of the Adal Sultanate into Aussa and the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Harar" title="Sultanate of Harar">Sultanate of Harar</a>. At some point after 1672, Aussa declined in conjunction with Imam Umar Din bin Adam's recorded ascension to the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1734, the <a href="/wiki/Afar_people" title="Afar people">Afar</a> leader Kedafu, head of the Mudaito clan, seized power and established the <a href="/wiki/Mudaito_Dynasty" title="Mudaito Dynasty">Mudaito Dynasty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pankhurstteb_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pankhurstteb-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> This marked the start of a new and more sophisticated polity that would last into the colonial period.<sup id="cite_ref-Pankhurstteb_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pankhurstteb-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Italian Eritrea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg/220px-Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg/330px-Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg/440px-Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Italian_Eritrea_1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1922 map of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The boundaries of the present-day Eritrea nation state were established during the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>. In 1869<sup id="cite_ref-Ully_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ully-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> or ’70, the then ruling Sultan of <a href="/wiki/Raheita" title="Raheita" class="mw-redirect">Raheita</a> sold lands surrounding the Bay of <a href="/wiki/Assab" title="Assab">Assab</a> to the Rubattino Shipping Company.<sup id="cite_ref-EBAb_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBAb-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The area served as a <a href="/wiki/Coaling_station" title="Coaling station" class="mw-redirect">coaling station</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Shipping_lane" title="Shipping lane" class="mw-redirect">shipping lanes</a> introduced by the recently completed <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>. It had long been part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> <a href="/wiki/Habesh_Eyalet" title="Habesh Eyalet">Habesh Eyalet</a> centered in <a href="/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt" title="Khedivate of Egypt">Egypt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The first Italian settlers arrived in 1880.<sup id="cite_ref-EBAb_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBAb-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the vacuum that followed the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gallabat" title="Battle of Gallabat">1889 death</a> of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Ethiopia" title="Emperor of Ethiopia">Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Yohannes_IV" title="Yohannes IV">Yohannes&#160;II</a>, Gen. <a href="/wiki/Oreste_Baratieri" title="Oreste Baratieri">Oreste Baratieri</a> occupied the highlands along the Eritrean coast and Italy proclaimed the establishment of the new colony of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a>, a colony of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Wuchale" title="Treaty of Wuchale">Treaty of Wuchale</a> (It.&#160;<i>Uccialli</i>) signed the same year, <a href="/wiki/Menelik_II" title="Menelik II">King Menelik</a> of <a href="/wiki/Shewa" title="Shewa">Shewa</a>, a southern Ethiopian kingdom, recognized the Italian occupation of his rivals' lands of <a href="/wiki/Bogos" title="Bogos" class="mw-redirect">Bogos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamasien" title="Hamasien">Hamasien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akkele_Guzay" title="Akkele Guzay" class="mw-redirect">Akkele Guzay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serae" title="Serae">Serae</a> in exchange for guarantees of financial assistance and continuing access to European arms and ammunition. His subsequent victory over his rival kings and enthronement as <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Ethiopia" title="Emperor of Ethiopia">Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Menelik_II_of_Ethiopia" title="Menelik II of Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect">Menelek&#160;II</a> (r.&#160;1889–1913) made the treaty formally binding upon the entire territory.<sup id="cite_ref-EBA_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBA-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg/220px-Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg/330px-Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg/440px-Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiat_Tagliero_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Tagliero_Building" title="Fiat Tagliero Building">Fiat Tagliero Building</a> in Asmara, built in 1938.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1888, the Italian administration launched its first development projects in the new colony. The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a> was completed to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saati&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Saati (page does not exist)">Saati</a> in 1888,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> and reached <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> in the highlands in 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-f1_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f1-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Asmara-Massawa_Cableway" title="Asmara-Massawa Cableway">Asmara–Massawa Cableway</a> was the longest line in the world during its time, but was later dismantled by the British in World War II. Besides major infrastructural projects, the colonial authorities invested significantly in the agricultural sector. It also oversaw the provision of urban amenities in Asmara and Massawa, and employed many Eritreans in public service, particularly in the police and public works departments.<sup id="cite_ref-f1_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f1-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Thousands of Eritreans were concurrently enlisted in the army, serving during the <a href="/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War" title="Italo-Turkish War">Italo-Turkish War</a> in Libya as well as the <a href="/wiki/First_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="First Italo-Ethiopian War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">second</a> Italo-Abyssinian Wars.</p>
<p>Additionally, the Italian Eritrea administration opened a number of new factories, which produced buttons, cooking oil, pasta, construction materials, packing meat, tobacco, hide and other household commodities. In 1939, there were around 2,198 factories and most of the employees were Eritrean citizens. The establishment of industries also made an increase in the number of both Italians and Eritreans residing in the cities. The number of Italians residing in the territory increased from 4,600 to 75,000 in five years; and with the involvement of Eritreans in the industries, trade and fruit plantation was expanded across the nation, while some of the plantations were owned by Eritreans.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1922, <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>'s rise to power in Italy brought profound changes to the colonial government in Italian Eritrea. After <i><a href="/wiki/Il_Duce" title="Il Duce" class="mw-redirect">il Duce</a></i> declared the birth of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Empire" title="Italian Empire">Italian Empire</a> in May 1936, Italian Eritrea (enlarged with northern Ethiopia's regions) and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a> were merged with the just conquered Ethiopia in the new <a href="/wiki/Italian_East_Africa" title="Italian East Africa">Italian East Africa</a> (<i>Africa Orientale Italiana</i>) administrative territory. This <a href="/wiki/Fascists" title="Fascists" class="mw-redirect">Fascist</a> period was characterized by imperial expansion in the name of a "new Roman Empire". Eritrea was chosen by the Italian government to be the industrial center of Italian East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_administration">British administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: British administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AsmaraStazione.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/AsmaraStazione.jpg/220px-AsmaraStazione.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/AsmaraStazione.jpg/330px-AsmaraStazione.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/AsmaraStazione.jpg/440px-AsmaraStazione.jpg 2x" data-file-width="524" data-file-height="305" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AsmaraStazione.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An Asmara station on the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a> (1938).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Through the 1941 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Keren" title="Battle of Keren">Battle of Keren</a>, the British expelled the Italians,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> and took over the administration of the country.</p>
<p>The British placed Eritrea under British military administration until <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied forces</a> could determine its fate. The first thing the British did was to dismantle and confiscate the Eritrean industries as war compensation, including parts of the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-Cpiehtmoeti_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cpiehtmoeti-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the absence of agreement amongst the Allies concerning the status of Eritrea, British administration continued for the remainder of World War II and until 1950. During the immediate postwar years, the British proposed that Eritrea be divided along religious lines and annexed to Sudan and Ethiopia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, anticipating a <a href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist" class="mw-redirect">communist</a> victory in the Italian polls, initially supported returning Eritrea to Italy under trusteeship or as a colony.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Arab states, seeing Eritrea as an extension of the Arab world, sought the establishment of an independent state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federation_with_Ethiopia">Federation with Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Federation with Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Eritrea_(1952-1961).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Flag_of_Eritrea_%281952-1961%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Eritrea_%281952-1961%29.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Flag_of_Eritrea_%281952-1961%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Eritrea_%281952-1961%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Flag_of_Eritrea_%281952-1961%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Eritrea_%281952-1961%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Eritrea_(1952-1961).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Eritrea" title="Flag of Eritrea">Flag of Eritrea</a> (1952–1961)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1950s, the Ethiopian feudal administration under Emperor <a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie_of_Ethiopia" title="Haile Selassie of Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect">Haile Selassie</a> sought to annex Eritrea and Italian Somaliland. He laid claim to both territories in a letter to Franklin D. Roosevelt at the Paris Peace Conference and at the First Session of the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-un_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United Nations, the debate over the fate of the former Italian colonies continued. The British and Americans preferred to cede all of Eritrea except the Western province to the Ethiopians as a reward for their support during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The Independence Bloc of Eritrean parties consistently requested from the UN General Assembly that a referendum be held immediately to settle the Eritrean question of sovereignty.</p>
<p>Following the adoption of <a href="//en.wikisource.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_390" class="extiw" title="s:United Nations General Assembly Resolution 390">UN Resolution 390A(V)</a> in December 1950, Eritrea was <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federated</a> with Ethiopia under the prompting of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-UNGA390_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNGA390-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The resolution called for Eritrea and Ethiopia to be linked through a loose federal structure under the sovereignty of the Emperor. Eritrea was to have its own administrative and judicial structure, its own flag, and control over its domestic affairs, including police, local administration, and taxation.<sup id="cite_ref-un_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The federal government, which for all intents and purposes was the existing imperial government, was to control foreign affairs (including commerce), defense, finance, and transportation. The resolution ignored the wishes of Eritreans for independence, but guaranteed the population democratic rights and a measure of autonomy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg/220px-War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg/330px-War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg/440px-War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="896" data-file-height="573" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:War_Memory_Square_in_Massawa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Independence Square in Massawa.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1958, a group of Eritreans based in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> founded the Eritrean Liberation Movement (ELM). The organization mainly consisted of Eritrean students, professionals and intellectuals. Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Idris_Awate" title="Hamid Idris Awate">Hamid Idris Awate</a>, it engaged in clandestine political activities intended to cultivate resistance to the centralizing policies of the imperial Ethiopian state.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> However, by 1962, the ELM had been discovered and destroyed by imperial authorities.</p>
<p>When Emperor Haile Selassie unilaterally dissolved the Eritrean parliament and illegally annexed the country in 1962, the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean Liberation Front">Eritrean Liberation Front</a> (ELF) waged an armed struggle for independence. The ensuing <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_for_Independence" title="Eritrean War for Independence" class="mw-redirect">Eritrean War for Independence</a> went on for 30 years against successive Ethiopian governments until 1991, when the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_People%27s_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean People's Liberation Front">Eritrean People's Liberation Front</a> (EPLF), a successor of the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean Liberation Front">ELF</a>, defeated the Ethiopian forces in Eritrea and helped a coalition of <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_People%27s_Revolutionary_Democratic_Front" title="Ethiopian People's Revolutionary Democratic Front">Ethiopian rebel forces</a> take control of the Ethiopian Capital <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>.</p>
<p>Following a UN-supervised <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_independence_referendum,_1993" title="Eritrean independence referendum, 1993">referendum in Eritrea</a> (dubbed <a href="/wiki/UNOVER" title="UNOVER" class="mw-redirect">UNOVER</a>) in which the Eritrean people overwhelmingly voted for independence, Eritrea declared its independence and gained international recognition in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Eritrea" title="Geography of Eritrea">Geography of Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Eritrea-CIA_WFB_Map.png/220px-Eritrea-CIA_WFB_Map.png" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8c/Eritrea-CIA_WFB_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8c/Eritrea-CIA_WFB_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="353" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eritrea is on the Red Sea and includes the <a href="/wiki/Dahlak_Archipelago" title="Dahlak Archipelago">Dahlak Archipelago</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_habitat">Location and habitat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Location and habitat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Highlands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Eritrean_Highlands.jpg/220px-Eritrean_Highlands.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Eritrean_Highlands.jpg/330px-Eritrean_Highlands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Eritrean_Highlands.jpg/440px-Eritrean_Highlands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Highlands.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_highlands" title="Eritrean highlands" class="mw-redirect">Eritrean highlands</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eritrea is located in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>. It is bordered to the northeast and east by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> to the east. Eritrea lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_north" title="12th parallel north">12°</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_north" title="18th parallel north">18°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/36th_meridian_east" title="36th meridian east">36°</a> and <a href="/wiki/44th_meridian_east" title="44th meridian east">44°E</a>.</p>
<p>The country is virtually bisected by a branch of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Rift" title="East African Rift">East African Rift</a>. It has fertile lands to the west, descending to desert in the east. Eritrea, at the southern end of the Red Sea, is the home of the fork in the rift. The <a href="/wiki/Dahlak_Archipelago" title="Dahlak Archipelago">Dahlak Archipelago</a> and its fishing grounds are situated off the sandy and arid coastline.</p>
<p>Eritrea can be split into three basic ecoregions. To the east of the highlands are the hot, arid coastal plains stretching down to the southeast of the country. The cooler, more fertile highlands, reaching up to 3000m has different habitat. Habitats here vary from the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">sub-tropical rainforest</a> at Filfil Solomona to the precipitous cliffs and <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">canyons</a> of the southern highlands.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG/220px-Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG/330px-Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG/440px-Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mountains_near_Asmara.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mountains near <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The strategically important <a href="/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb" title="Bab-el-Mandeb">Bab-el-Mandeb</a> strait connects the coasts of Eritrea and Yemen. The <a href="/wiki/Afar_Triangle" title="Afar Triangle">Afar Triangle</a> or Danakil Depression of Eritrea is the probable location of a <a href="/wiki/Triple_junction" title="Triple junction">triple junction</a> where three tectonic plates are pulling away from one another: the Arabian Plate, and the two parts of the African Plate (the Nubian and the Somali plate) splitting along the East African Rift Zone (USGS). The highest point of the country, <a href="/wiki/Emba_Soira" title="Emba Soira">Emba Soira</a>, is located in the center of Eritrea, at 3,018 meters (9,902&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level" class="mw-redirect">above sea level</a>.</p>
<p>The main cities of the country are the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> and the port town of <a href="/wiki/Asseb" title="Asseb" class="mw-redirect">Asseb</a> in the southeast, as well as the towns of <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> to the east, the northern town of <a href="/wiki/Keren,_Eritrea" title="Keren, Eritrea">Keren</a>, and the central town <a href="/wiki/Mendefera" title="Mendefera">Mendefera</a>.</p>
<p>In 2006, Eritrea announced it would become the first country in the world to turn its entire coast into an environmentally protected zone. The 1,347&#160;km (837&#160;mi) coastline, along with another 1,946&#160;km (1,209&#160;mi) of coast around its more than 350 islands, will come under governmental protection.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Eritrea" title="Wildlife of Eritrea">Wildlife of Eritrea</a></div>
<p><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_in_Eritrea" title="List of mammals in Eritrea" class="mw-redirect">List of mammals in Eritrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Eritrea" title="List of birds of Eritrea">List of birds of Eritrea</a></i> Eritrea has several of mammals and a rich avifauna of 560 species of birds.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG/220px-Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG/330px-Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG/440px-Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1689" data-file-height="1266" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nymphalidae_-_Precis_pelarga.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Precis_pelarga" title="Precis pelarga">Precis pelarga</a> specimen from Eritrea.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eritrea is home to an abundant amount of big game species. Enforced regulations have helped in steadily increasing their numbers throughout Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Mammals commonly seen today include the <a href="/wiki/Abyssinian_hare" title="Abyssinian hare">Abyssinian hare</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_wild_cat" title="African wild cat" class="mw-redirect">African wild cat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black-backed_jackal" title="Black-backed jackal">Black-backed jackal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_jackal" title="Golden jackal">golden jackal</a>, Genet, <a href="/wiki/Ground_squirrel" title="Ground squirrel">Ground squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pale_fox" title="Pale fox">pale fox</a>, Soemmering’s gazelle, <a href="/wiki/Warthog" title="Warthog">warthog</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dorcas_gazelle" title="Dorcas gazelle">Dorcas gazelle</a> are common on the coastal plains and in Gash Barka.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lions" title="Lions" class="mw-redirect">Lions</a> are said to inhabit the mountains of the Gash-Barka Region. There is also a small population of <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephants</a> that roam in some parts of the country. Dik-diks can also be found in many areas. The endangered <a href="/wiki/African_wild_ass" title="African wild ass">African wild ass</a> can be seen in Denakalia Region. Other local wildlife include bushbucks, duikers, greater kudus, klipspringers, <a href="/wiki/Leopards" title="Leopards" class="mw-redirect">leopards</a>, oryxs and crocodiles.,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ibis.atwebpages.com_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibis.atwebpages.com-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spotted_hyena" title="Spotted hyena">spotted hyena</a> is widespread and fairly common. Between 1955 and 2001 there were no reported sightings of elephant herds, and they are thought to have fallen victim to the war of independence. In December 2001 a herd of about 30, including 10 juveniles, was observed in the vicinity of the <a href="/wiki/Gash_River" title="Gash River" class="mw-redirect">Gash River</a>. The elephants seemed to have formed a <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">symbiotic</a> relationship with <a href="/wiki/Olive_baboon" title="Olive baboon">olive baboons</a>, with the baboons using the water holes dug by the elephants, while the elephants use the tree-top baboons as an early warning system.</p>
<p>It is estimated that there are around 100 elephants left in Eritrea, the most northerly of East Africa's elephants.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Endangered" title="Endangered" class="mw-redirect">endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/Painted_hunting_dog" title="Painted hunting dog" class="mw-redirect">painted hunting dog</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Lycaon_pictus" title="Lycaon pictus" class="mw-redirect">Lycaon pictus</a></i>) was previously found in Eritrea, but is now deemed extirpated from the entire country.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In Gash Barka, deadly snakes like <a href="/wiki/Echis_pyramidum" title="Echis pyramidum">saw-scaled viper</a> are common. <a href="/wiki/Bitis_arietans" title="Bitis arietans">Puff adder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_spitting_cobra" title="Red spitting cobra">red spitting cobra</a> are widespread and can be found even in the highlands.In the coastal areas marine species that are common include dolphin, <a href="/wiki/Dugong" title="Dugong">dugong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whale_shark" title="Whale shark">whale shark</a>, turtles, marlin/swordfish, and manta ray.<sup id="cite_ref-ibis.atwebpages.com_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibis.atwebpages.com-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Eritrea" title="Politics of Eritrea">Politics of Eritrea</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Front_for_Democracy_and_Justice" title="People's Front for Democracy and Justice">People's Front for Democracy and Justice</a> (PFDJ) is the ruling party in Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Other political groups are not allowed to organize, although the unimplemented Constitution of 1997 provides for the existence of multi-party politics. The National Assembly has 150 seats, of which 75 are occupied by the PFDJ. National elections have been periodically scheduled and cancelled; none have ever been held in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The president, <a href="/wiki/Isaias_Afwerki" title="Isaias Afwerki">Isaias Afwerki</a>, has been in office since independence in 1993.</p>
<p>Independent local sources of political information on Eritrean domestic politics are scarce; in September 2001 the government closed down all of the nation's privately owned print <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">media</a>, and <a href="/wiki/G-15" title="G-15" class="mw-redirect">outspoken critics of the government</a> have been arrested and held without trial, according to various international observers, including <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004 the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> declared Eritrea a <a href="/wiki/Country_of_Particular_Concern" title="Country of Particular Concern">Country of Particular Concern</a> (CPC) for its record of <a href="/wiki/Religious_persecution" title="Religious persecution">religious persecution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_elections">National elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: National elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Government_building,_Asmara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg/220px-Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg/330px-Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg/440px-Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1278" data-file-height="847" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Government_building,_Asmara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Building of regional administration in <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eritrean National elections were set for 2001 but was then decided that because 20% of Eritrea's land was under occupation, elections would be postponed until the resolution of the conflict with Ethiopia. However, local elections have continued in Eritrea. The most recent round of local government elections were held in 2010 and 2011. On further elections, the President's Chief of Staff, Yemane Gebremeskel said,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The electoral commission is handling these elections this time round so that may be the new element in this process. The national assembly has also mandated the electoral commission to set the date for national elections, so whenever the electoral commission sets the date there will be national elections. It's not dependent on regional elections.</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>As yet, no national elections have been held since independence.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_districts">Regions and districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Regions and districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Eritrea.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Regions_of_Eritrea.svg/220px-Regions_of_Eritrea.svg.png" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Regions_of_Eritrea.svg/330px-Regions_of_Eritrea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Regions_of_Eritrea.svg/440px-Regions_of_Eritrea.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="409" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Eritrea.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Regions of Eritrea</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Un-eritrea.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Un-eritrea.png/300px-Un-eritrea.png" width="300" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Un-eritrea.png/450px-Un-eritrea.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Un-eritrea.png/600px-Un-eritrea.png 2x" data-file-width="3038" data-file-height="2257" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Un-eritrea.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Eritrea</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Eritrea" title="Regions of Eritrea">Regions of Eritrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Eritrea" title="Districts of Eritrea" class="mw-redirect">Districts of Eritrea</a></div>
<p>Eritrea is divided into six administrative <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Eritrea" title="Regions of Eritrea">regions</a> (<i>zoba</i>). These are further subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Subregions_of_Eritrea" title="Subregions of Eritrea">subregions</a> (<i>sub-zoba</i>). The geographical extent of the regions is based on their respective hydrological properties. This is a dual intent on the part of the Eritrean government: to provide each administrative region with sufficient control over its agricultural capacity, and to eliminate historical intra-regional conflicts.<br style="clear:both;" />
The administrative regions followed by the sub-region are:</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<th>No.</th>
