<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Defence_Forces" title="Eritrean Defence Forces">Eritrean Defence Forces</a> are the official <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> of the State of Eritrea.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Eritrea" title="Human rights in Eritrea">Human rights in Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:October15kabine1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/October15kabine1.jpg/220px-October15kabine1.jpg" width="220" height="295" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/October15kabine1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/October15kabine1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="335" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:October15kabine1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President of Eritrea <a href="/wiki/Isaias_Afwerki" title="Isaias Afwerki">Isaias Afwerki</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eritrea is a <a href="/wiki/Single-party_state" title="Single-party state">single-party state</a> in which national legislative elections have been repeatedly postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Human Rights Watch, the government's <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> record is considered among the worst in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Some Western countries, particularly the United States, have in particular accused the Eritrean authorities of arbitrary arrest and detentions, and of detaining an unknown number of people without charge for their political activism. However, the Eritrean government has continuously dismissed the accusations as politically motivated.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Since Eritrea's conflict with <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> in 1998–2001, the nation's human rights record has come under criticism at the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Human rights violations are allegedly frequently committed by the government or on behalf of the government. <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">Freedom of speech</a>, <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">press</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly" title="Freedom of assembly">assembly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interpersonal_relationship" title="Interpersonal relationship">association</a> are limited. Those who practice "unregistered" religions, try to flee the nation, or escape military duty are arrested and put into <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">prison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>All Eritreans between the ages of 18–40 must complete a mandatory national service, which includes military service. This national service was implemented after Eritrea gained its <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> from Ethiopia, as a precautionary means to be protected against any threats on Eritrea’s <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a>, to instill national pride, and to improve the country's small economy. Eritrea’s national service requires lengthy, indefinite conscription periods, which some Eritreans leave the country in order to avoid.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As an attempt at reform, Eritrean government officials and NGO representatives have participated in numerous public meetings and dialogues. In these sessions they have answered questions as fundamental as, "What are human rights?", "Who determines what are human rights?", and "What should take precedence, human or communal rights?"<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, the Eritrean government also banned <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> In Regional Assemblies and religious circles, Eritreans themselves speak out continuously against the use of female circumcision. They cite health concerns and individual freedom as being of primary concern when they say this. Furthermore they implore rural peoples to cast away this ancient cultural practice.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, a new movement called Citizens for Democratic Rights in Eritrea aimed at bringing about dialogue between the government and opposition was formed in early 2009. The group consists of ordinary citizens and some people close to the government.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_freedom">Media freedom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Media freedom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In its 2014 Press Freedom Index, <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> ranked the media environment in Eritrea at the very bottom of a list of 178 countries, just below totalitarian <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, "Eritrea is the only African country to have no privately owned news media",<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> and Reporters Without Borders said of the public media, "[they] do nothing but relay the regime's belligerent and ultra-nationalist discourse. ... Not a single [foreign correspondent] now lives in Asmara."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The state-owned news agency censors news about external events.<sup id="cite_ref-censored_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censored-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Independent media have been banned since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-censored_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censored-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Eritrea" title="Foreign relations of Eritrea">Foreign relations of Eritrea</a></div>
<p>Eritrea is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, and is an <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Eritrean_relations" title="Arab–Eritrean relations">observing member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>. The nation holds a seat on the United Nations' Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions (ACABQ). Eritrea also holds memberships in the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">International Finance Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Police_Organization" title="International Criminal Police Organization" class="mw-redirect">International Criminal Police Organization</a> (INTERPOL), <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organization for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons" class="mw-redirect">Organization for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Customs_Organization" title="World Customs Organization">World Customs Organization</a>.</p>
<p>The Eritrean government previously withdrew its representative to the African Union to protest the AU's alleged lack of leadership in facilitating the implementation of a binding border decision demarcating the border between Eritrea and Ethiopia. The Eritrean government has since January 2011 appointed an envoy, Tesfa-Alem Tekle, to the AU.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Eritrea maintains diplomatic ties with a number of other countries, including <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China%E2%80%93Eritrea_relations" title="People's Republic of China–Eritrea relations" class="mw-redirect">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Eritrea_relations" title="Denmark–Eritrea relations">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djibouti%E2%80%93Eritrea_relations" title="Djibouti–Eritrea relations">Djibouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eritrea%E2%80%93Israel_relations" title="Eritrea–Israel relations">Israel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eritrea%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Eritrea–United States relations">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrea%E2%80%93Yemen_relations" title="Eritrea–Yemen relations">Yemen</a>. Its relations with Djibouti and Yemen are tense due to territorial disputes over the <a href="/wiki/Doumeira_Islands" title="Doumeira Islands">Doumeira Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanish_Islands" title="Hanish Islands">Hanish Islands</a>, respectively.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_Ethiopia">Relations with Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Relations with Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War" title="Eritrean–Ethiopian War">Eritrean–Ethiopian War</a></div>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_independence_referendum,_1993" title="Eritrean independence referendum, 1993">Eritrean independence referendum, 1993</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png/220px-Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png/330px-Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png/440px-Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1642" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War_Map_1998.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War" title="Eritrean–Ethiopian War">Eritrean–Ethiopian War</a> map, 1998.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The undemarcated border with Ethiopia is the primary external issue currently facing Eritrea. Eritrea's relations with Ethiopia turned from that of cautious mutual tolerance, following the 30-year war for Eritrean independence, to a deadly rivalry that led to the outbreak of hostilities from May 1998 to June 2000 which claimed approximately 70,000 casualties from both sides.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The border conflict cost hundreds of millions of dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Disagreements following the war have resulted in stalemate punctuated by periods of elevated tension and renewed threats of war.<sup id="cite_ref-horntension1_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horntension1-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-horntension3_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horntension3-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The stalemate led the President of Eritrea to urge the UN to take action on Ethiopia with the <a href="//en.wikisource.org/wiki/Eleven_Letters" class="extiw" title="s:Eleven Letters">Eleven Letters</a> penned by the President to the United Nations Security Council. The situation has been further escalated by the continued efforts of the Eritrean and Ethiopian leaders in supporting opposition in one another's countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2011, Ethiopia accused Eritrea of planting bombs at an <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> summit in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, which was later supported by a UN report. Eritrea denied the claims.<sup id="cite_ref-aubomb_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aubomb-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Eritrea" title="Economy of Eritrea">Economy of Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_Eritrea" title="List of companies based in Eritrea">List of companies based in Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="860" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_exports_2009_Eritrea.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eritrea's main export distribution</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The economy of Eritrea has experienced considerable growth in recent years, indicated by an improvement in gross domestic product (GDP) in October 2012 of 7.5 percent over 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> A big reason for the recent growth of the Eritrean economy is the commencement of full operations in the gold and silver Bisha mine and the production of cement from the cement factory in Massawa.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The real GDP (2009 est.): $4.4 billion, and the annual growth rate (2011 est.):14%.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>However, worker <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> from abroad are estimated to account for 32 percent of gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Eritrea has an extensive amount of resources such as copper, gold, granite, marble, and potash. The Eritrean economy has undergone extreme changes due to the War of Independence. In 2011, Eritrea's GDP grew by 8.7 percent making it one of the fastest growing economies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The Economist Intelligence Unit (EIU) expects it to maintain a high growth rate of 8.5 percent in 2013.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War" title="Eritrean–Ethiopian War">Eritrean–Ethiopian War</a> severely hurt Eritrea's economy. <a href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" title="Gross Domestic Product" class="mw-redirect">GDP</a> growth in 1999 fell to less than 1%, and GDP decreased by 8.2% in 2000. In May 2000, the war resulted in some $600 million in property damage and loss, including losses of $225 million in <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> and 55,000 homes.</p>
<p>Even during the war, Eritrea developed its <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Eritrea" title="Transport in Eritrea">transportation infrastructure</a> by asphalting new roads, improving its ports, and repairing war-damaged roads and bridges as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Wefri_Warsay_Yika%27alo" title="Wefri Warsay Yika'alo">Warsay Yika'alo Program</a>. The most significant of these projects was the construction of a coastal highway of more than 500&#160;km connecting <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> with <a href="/wiki/Asseb" title="Asseb" class="mw-redirect">Asseb</a>, as well as the rehabilitation of the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a>. The rail line has been restored between the port of Massawa and the capital Asmara, although services are sporadic. Steam locomotives are sometimes used for groups of enthusiasts.</p>
<p>In theory, the country has a national carrier, <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Airlines" title="Eritrean Airlines">Eritrean Airlines</a>, but services are intermittent.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Eritrea" title="Demographics of Eritrea">Demographics of Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg/170px-Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg" width="170" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg/255px-Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg/340px-Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1211" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eritrean women performing a traditional <a href="/wiki/Tigray-Tigrinya_people" title="Tigray-Tigrinya people">Tigrinya</a> dance.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are nine recognized ethnic groups according to the government of Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Eritrean society is ethnically <a href="/wiki/Homogeneity_and_heterogeneity" title="Homogeneity and heterogeneity">heterogeneous</a>. An independent census has yet to be conducted, but the <a href="/wiki/Tigrinya_people" title="Tigrinya people" class="mw-redirect">Tigrinya people</a> make up about 55% and <a href="/wiki/Tigre_people" title="Tigre people">Tigre people</a> make up about 30% of the population. These form the bulk of the country's predominantly <a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a>-speaking population. Most of the rest of the population belong to other <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a>-speaking communities of the <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branch, such as the <a href="/wiki/Saho_people" title="Saho people">Saho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedareb_people" title="Hedareb people">Hedareb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afar_people" title="Afar people">Afar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bilen_people" title="Bilen people">Bilen</a>.</p>
<p>Other Afroasiatic groups include the <a href="/wiki/Rashaida_people" title="Rashaida people">Rashaida</a>, who represent about 2% of Eritrea's population.<sup id="cite_ref-Ciaethn_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ciaethn-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> They reside in the northern coastal lowlands of Eritrea as well as the eastern coasts of Sudan. The Rashaida first came to Eritrea in the 19th century from the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> More recently, <a href="/wiki/Hadhrami_people" title="Hadhrami people">Hadhrami</a> migrants have also settled in the country.</p>
<p>There are also a number of <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotic</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minority" title="Ethnic minority" class="mw-redirect">ethnic minorities</a>, who are represented in Eritrea by the <a href="/wiki/Kunama_people" title="Kunama people">Kunama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nara_people" title="Nara people">Nara</a>. Each ethnicity speaks a different native tongue but, typically, many of the minorities speak more than one language.</p>
<p>In addition, there exist <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritreans" title="Italian Eritreans">Italian Eritrean</a> (concentrated in Asmara) and Ethiopian Tigrayan communities. Neither is generally given citizenship unless through marriage or, more rarely, by having it conferred upon them by the State.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Eritrea" title="Languages of Eritrea">Languages of Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Women.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Eritrean_Women.jpeg/220px-Eritrean_Women.jpeg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Eritrean_Women.jpeg/330px-Eritrean_Women.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Eritrean_Women.jpeg/440px-Eritrean_Women.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="849" data-file-height="566" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Women.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Saho_people" title="Saho people">Saho</a> women in traditional attire.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eritrea is a multilingual country. The nation has no official language, as the Constitution establishes the "equality of all Eritrean languages".<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Tigrinya_language" title="Tigrinya language">Tigrinya</a> serve as de facto language of national identity. With 2,540,000 total speakers of a population of 5,254,000 in 2006, Tigrinya is the most widely spoken language; particularly in the southern and central parts of Eritrea. <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a> serves as de facto national language. <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> also serves as a de facto national working language, and there are a few monolinguals of <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethner_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethner-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the languages spoken in Eritrea stem from the <a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> Among these are <a href="/wiki/Tigre_language" title="Tigre language">Tigre</a>, Tigrinya, the newly recognized <a href="/wiki/Dahlik_language" title="Dahlik language" class="mw-redirect">Dahlik</a>, and Arabic (the <a href="/wiki/Hejazi_Arabic" title="Hejazi Arabic">Hejazi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hadhrami_Arabic" title="Hadhrami Arabic">Hadhrami</a> <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Arabic" title="Varieties of Arabic">dialects</a> spoken by the Rashaida and Hadhrami, respectively). Other Afroasiatic languages belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branch are also widely spoken in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> The latter include <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beja_language" title="Beja language">Beja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blin_language" title="Blin language" class="mw-redirect">Blin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saho_language" title="Saho language">Saho</a>.</p>
<p>In addition, <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kunama_language" title="Kunama language">Kunama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nara_language" title="Nara language">Nara</a>) are also spoken as a <a href="/wiki/Native_language" title="Native language" class="mw-redirect">native language</a> by the Nilotic Kunama and Nara ethnic minority groups that live in the northern and northwestern part of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>English is also spoken as a working language used in secondary and university education.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>According to recent estimates, 50% of the population adheres to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> 48%, while 2% of the population follows other <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religions</a> including <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religion" title="Traditional African religion">traditional African religion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-webcitation.org_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webcitation.org-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> According to a study made by <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 63% adheres to Christianity and 36% adheres to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-pewforum.org_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewforum.org-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Since May 2002, the government of Eritrea has officially recognized the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Orthodox_Tewahedo_Church" title="Eritrean Orthodox Tewahedo Church">Eritrean Orthodox Tewahedo Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>, Catholicism, and the Evangelical <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran" class="mw-redirect">Lutheran</a> church. All other faiths and denominations are required to undergo a registration process.<sup id="cite_ref-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Among other things, the government's registration system requires religious groups to submit personal information on their membership to be allowed to <a href="/wiki/Worship" title="Worship">worship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Cathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Catholic_Cathedral.jpg/220px-Catholic_Cathedral.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Catholic_Cathedral.jpg/330px-Catholic_Cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Catholic_Cathedral.jpg/440px-Catholic_Cathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Cathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_Cathedral,_Asmara" title="St. Joseph's Cathedral, Asmara">St. Joseph's Cathedral</a> church in the capital <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_(8529064326).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg/220px-Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg/330px-Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg/440px-Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_(8529064326).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 15th century Sheikh Hanafi Mosque in <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Eritrean government is against reformed or radical versions of its established religions. Therefore, radical forms of Islam and Christianity (viz, Salafism), <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a> (though the Bahá'í Faith is neither Islamic nor Christian), the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, and numerous other non-Protestant Evangelical denominations are not registered and cannot worship freely. Three named Jehovah's Witnesses are known to have been imprisoned since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2006, there was only one native adherent of <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, Sami Cohen, remaining in Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In its 2006 religious freedom report, the U.S. State Department named Eritrea a "Country of Particular Concern" (CPC) for the third year in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Eritrea" title="Health in Eritrea">Health in Eritrea</a></div>
<p>Eritrea has achieved significant improvements in health care and is one of the few countries to be on target to meet its <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goal" title="Millennium Development Goal" class="mw-redirect">Millennium Development Goal</a> (MDG) targets in health, in particular child health.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth has increased from 39.1 in 1960 to 59.5 years in 2008, maternal and <a href="/wiki/Child_mortality" title="Child mortality">child mortality</a> rates have dropped dramatically and the health infrastructure has been expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to Eritrea's relative isolation, information and resources are extremely limited and according the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organisation</a> (WHO) found in 2008 average life expectancy to be slightly less than 63 years. <a href="/wiki/Immunization" title="Immunization">Immunisation</a> and child nutrition has been tackled by working closely with schools in a multi-sectoral approach; the number of children vaccinated against measles almost doubled in seven years, from 40.7% to 78.5% and the underweight prevalence among children decreased by 12% in 1995–2002 (severe underweight prevalence by 28%).<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The National Malaria Protection Unit of the Ministry of Health has registered tremendous improvements in reducing malarial mortality by as much as 85% and the number of cases by 92% between 1998 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The Eritrean government has banned <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> (FGM), saying the practice was painful and put women at risk of life-threatening health problems.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>However, Eritrea still faces many challenges. Despite number of physicians increasing from only 0.2 in 1993 to 0.5 in 2004 per 1000 population, this is still very low.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_114-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> are common in Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> HIV prevalence among the 15–49 group exceeds 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> The fertility rate is at about 5 births per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Maternal mortality dropped by more than half from 1995 to 2002, although the figure is still high.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_114-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly, between 1995 and 2002, the number of births attended by skilled health personnel has doubled but still is only 28.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_114-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> A major cause of death in neonates is by severe <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Per capita expenditure on health is low in Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_116-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Eritrea" title="Education in Eritrea">Education in Eritrea</a></div>
<p>There are five levels of education in Eritrea: <a href="/wiki/Preschool_education" title="Preschool education" class="mw-redirect">pre-primary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">post-secondary</a>. There are nearly 238,000 students in the primary, middle, and secondary levels of education. There are approximately 824 schools<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> in Eritrea and two universities (the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Asmara" title="University of Asmara">University of Asmara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eritrea_Institute_of_Technology" title="Eritrea Institute of Technology">Eritrea Institute of Technology</a>) as well as several smaller colleges and technical schools.</p>
<p>Education in Eritrea is officially compulsory between seven and 13 years of age. However, the education infrastructure is inadequate to meet current needs. Statistics vary at the elementary level, suggesting that between 65 and 70% of school-aged children attend primary school; Approximately 61% attend secondary school. Student-teacher ratios are high: 45 to 1 at the elementary level and 54 to 1 at the secondary level. There are an average 63 students per classroom at the elementary level and 97 per classroom at the secondary level. Learning hours at school are often less than six hours per day. Skill shortages are present at all levels of the education system, and funding for and access to education vary significantly by gender and location. Illiteracy estimates for Eritrea range from around 40% to as high as 70%.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Barriers to education in Eritrea include traditional <a href="/wiki/Taboos" title="Taboos" class="mw-redirect">taboos</a>, school fees (for registration and materials), and the <a href="/wiki/Opportunity_costs" title="Opportunity costs" class="mw-redirect">opportunity costs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Low-income" title="Low-income" class="mw-redirect">low-income</a> households.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Eritrea" title="Culture of Eritrea">Culture of Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coffee_ceremony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Coffee_ceremony.jpg/220px-Coffee_ceremony.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Coffee_ceremony.jpg/330px-Coffee_ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d5/Coffee_ceremony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coffee_ceremony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An Eritrean woman pouring traditionally brewed coffee into <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finjal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Finjal (page does not exist)">finjal</a> from a <a href="/wiki/Jebena" title="Jebena">jebena</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The culture of Eritrea has been largely shaped by the country's location on the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> coast. One of the most recognizable parts of Eritrean culture is the <a href="/wiki/Coffee_ceremony" title="Coffee ceremony">coffee ceremony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Coffee (<a href="/wiki/Ge%27ez_alphabet" title="Ge'ez alphabet" class="mw-redirect">Ge'ez</a> ቡን <i>būn</i>) is offered when visiting friends, during festivities, or as a daily staple of life. If it is politely declined, then most likely <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a> ("shai" ሻሂ <i>shahee</i>) will instead be served.</p>
<p>Traditional Eritrean attire is quite varied among the different ethnic groups of Eritrea. In the big cities most of the people in the larger cities, dress casually clothes, with jeans, shirts, typically western. In offices both men and women often dress in suits. Traditional clothing for the <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> Tigrinya-speaking highlanders consists of bright white gowns called <i>zurias</i>, and the men wear long white shirts accompanied by white pants. Of the Muslim communities in the Eritrean lowland the women traditionally dress in brightly colored clothes. only Rashaida women maintain a tradition of covering half of their faces, but they do not cover their hair.</p>
<p>Besides convergent culinary tastes, Eritreans share an appreciation for similar music and lyrics, jewelry and fragrances, and tapestry and fabrics as other populations in the Horn region.<sup id="cite_ref-Tekle197_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tekle197-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kitcha_fit_fit.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Kitcha_fit_fit.png/170px-Kitcha_fit_fit.png" width="170" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Kitcha_fit_fit.png/255px-Kitcha_fit_fit.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Kitcha_fit_fit.png/340px-Kitcha_fit_fit.png 2x" data-file-width="828" data-file-height="868" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kitcha_fit_fit.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kitcha_fit-fit" title="Kitcha fit-fit" class="mw-redirect">Kitcha fit-fit</a> is a staple of <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Eritrea" title="Cuisine of Eritrea" class="mw-redirect">Eritrean cuisine</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_cuisine" title="Eritrean cuisine">Eritrean cuisine</a></div>
<p>A typical Eritrean dish consists of <a href="/wiki/Injera" title="Injera">injera</a> accompanied by a spicy stew, which frequently includes beef, kid, lamb or fish. <sup id="cite_ref-Kittler_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kittler-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Overall, Eritrean cuisine strongly resembles those of neighboring <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_cuisine" title="Ethiopian cuisine">Ethiopia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somali_cuisine" title="Somali cuisine">Somalia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kittler_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kittler-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tekle142_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tekle142-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> except for the fact that Eritrean and Somali cooking tend to feature more <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a> than Ethiopian cuisine on account of their coastal locations.<sup id="cite_ref-Kittler_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kittler-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Eritrean dishes are also frequently "lighter" in texture than Ethiopian meals. They likewise tend to employ less <a href="/wiki/Niter_kibbeh" title="Niter kibbeh">seasoned butter</a> and spices and more <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, as in the <i>tsebhi dorho</i> delicacy. Additionally, owing to its colonial history, cuisine in Eritrea features more <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> influences than are present in Ethiopian cooking, including more <a href="/wiki/Pasta" title="Pasta">pasta</a> and greater use of <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a> powders and <a href="/wiki/Cumin" title="Cumin">cumin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mftdbeaeccdtmts_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mftdbeaeccdtmts-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Alongside <i>sowa</i>, people in Eritrea also tend to drink coffee, whereas sweetened tea is preferred in Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-Kittler_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kittler-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Mies</i> is another popular local alcoholic beverage, made out of honey.<sup id="cite_ref-Mettm_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mettm-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Eritrea" title="Music of Eritrea">Music of Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Helen_Meles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Helen_Meles.jpg/170px-Helen_Meles.jpg" width="170" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Helen_Meles.jpg/255px-Helen_Meles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Helen_Meles.jpg/340px-Helen_Meles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1392" data-file-height="2138" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Helen_Meles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eritrean artist <a href="/wiki/Helen_Meles" title="Helen Meles">Helen Meles</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eritrea's various ethnic groups each have their own different styles of music and accompanying dances. Amongst the Tigrinya, the best known traditional musical genre is the guaila. Traditional instruments of Eritrean folk music include the stringed <a href="/wiki/Kraar" title="Kraar" class="mw-redirect">kraar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kebero" title="Kebero">kebero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyre" title="Lyre">lyre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kobar" title="Kobar">kobar</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wata&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wata (page does not exist)">wata</a> (a distant/rudimentary cousin of the violin). The most popular Eritrean artist is the Tigrinya singer <a href="/wiki/Helen_Meles" title="Helen Meles">Helen Meles</a>, who is noted for her powerful voice and wide singing range.<sup id="cite_ref-Blum_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blum-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Other prominent local musicians include the Kunama singer <a href="/wiki/Dehab_Faytinga" title="Dehab Faytinga">Dehab Faytinga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Abraha" title="Ruth Abraha">Ruth Abraha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bereket_Mengisteab" title="Bereket Mengisteab">Bereket Mengisteab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yemane_Baria" title="Yemane Baria">Yemane Baria</a>, and the late <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Afewerki" title="Abraham Afewerki">Abraham Afewerki</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Eritrea" title="Sport in Eritrea">Sport in Eritrea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tour_of_Eritrea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2a/Tour_of_Eritrea.jpg/220px-Tour_of_Eritrea.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2a/Tour_of_Eritrea.jpg/330px-Tour_of_Eritrea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2a/Tour_of_Eritrea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tour_of_Eritrea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cyclists competing in the <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Eritrea" title="Tour of Eritrea">Tour of Eritrea</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Eritrea" title="Tour of Eritrea">cycling</a> are the most popular sports in Eritrea. In recent years, Eritrean athletes have also seen increasing success in the international arena. <a href="/wiki/Zersenay_Tadese" title="Zersenay Tadese">Zersenay Tadese</a>, an Eritrean athlete, currently holds the world record in half marathon distance running.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Eritrea" title="Tour of Eritrea">Tour of Eritrea</a>, a multi-stage international cycling event, is held annually throughout the country. The Eritrea national cycling team has experienced a lot of success, winning the continental cycling championship several years in a row. Six Eritrean riders have been signed to international cycling teams, including <a href="/wiki/Natnael_Berhane" title="Natnael Berhane">Natnael Berhane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Teklehaimanot" title="Daniel Teklehaimanot">Daniel Teklehaimanot</a>. Berhane was the first Eritrean to compete in the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a>, and his performances earned him African Sportsman of the Year honors in 2013, while Teklehaimanot became the first Eritrean to ride the <a href="/wiki/Vuelta_a_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Vuelta a España">Vuelta a España</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Cnbcfertf_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cnbcfertf-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
